IN THE SUPREME COURT OF INDIA
CIVIL APPELLATE JURISDICTION

THE MANAGING DIRECTOR,

CORPORATION LTD. AND ANR.               APPELLANT(s)

A. MOHAN (DEAD) THR. LRS.                    RESPONDENT(s)
WITH
CIVIL APPEAL NO. 8742 OF 2015
TAMIL NADU INDUSTRIAL INVESTMENT

VERSUS
G. K. ANBU                                   RESPONDENT(s)
O R D E R
1) These  civil  appeals  assail  the  judgment  dated
23.03.2011  (hereinafter,  “impugned  judgement”)  of  the
Division Bench of the Madras High Court (hereinafter,
“High Court”) whereby, in Writ Appeal No. 722 of 2009, the
High Court set aside the order of enhancement of penalty
passed by appellant no.2 – Board of Directors (hereinafter
“Appellate Authority”) as confirmed by the learned Single
1

--- Page 20 ---
Judge in the case of respondent no.1 – A. Mohan, since
deceased. 
2) It shall be noted that the respondent no.1 – A. Mohan
passed away during the pendency of the appeal, and his
legal representatives (hereinafter “LRs”) were substituted
and brought on record by this Court  vide order dated
12.08.2024. Consequently, any reference to the respondent
shall be construed as a reference to his LRs, who shall be
entitled to the benefits of the instant order.  
3) The High Court,  vide the impugned judgement also
dismissed the Writ Appeal No. 738 of 2009, preferred by
the appellant no.1 – employer.  In the case of respondent
no.2 - G.K. Anbu, who was initially demoted by the
Disciplinary Authority, the Appellate Authority enhanced
the penalty to dismissal. This was set aside by the
learned Single Judge, maintaining the demotion and the
same  was  confirmed  in  writ  appeal  in  the  impugned
judgment. 
4) It is not out of place to mention that the impugned
judgment passed in the respective writ appeals is merely
an order of remand for consideration by the Appellate
Authority in the case of both respondents-employees. 
2

--- Page 21 ---
5) The limited question raised before us was that both
the  respondents-employees  have  been  dealt  with
inappropriately  and  discriminated  against  the  other
employee,  namely  A.  Muruganantham.  It  was  said  that
against all three employees, a common chargesheet was
issued on a similar thread of allegations. In response,
the Disciplinary Authority demoted A. Muruganantham who
was also a part of the common enquiry. He did not prefer
any appeal before the Appellate Authority, and as such,
the order of demotion was maintained against him.  
6) For  clarity,  the  punishment  imposed  on  the
respondents-employees, as well as A. Muruganantham, by the
different authorities is tabulated below:
Employee
Punishment
awarded by

awarded by

Authority

the High
Court

from

A. Muruganantham Demoted - - - 
7) At this stage, it is necessary to advert to the
reasons which weighed with the Division Bench of the High
Court  in  remitting  the  matter  only  in  the  case  of
3

--- Page 22 ---
respondent no.1 – A. Mohan (deceased). Such reasoning can
be found in paragraphs 19 and 21 of the impugned judgment,
which are reproduced below:
“19. The substance of charges framed against the
appellant in W.A. No. 722 of 2009 remains the
same as in the case of Tvl. Muruganantham and
Anbu.  In fact, summary of charges shows that
the  allegations  were  more  against  Thiru  A.
Muruganantham  than  against  other  officers.
However, for the reasons best known to the
management  they  have  given  only  lesser
punishment to Thiru A. Murugananthan.  It was
not the case of the Corporation that Thiru
Avl.A. Mohan was the main culprit and others
were only assisting him.  Similarly, it was not
their  case  that  the  nature  of  duties  and
responsibilities  of  the  delinquent  were
different and punishments were awarded depending
upon the culpability.  The charge sheet proceeds
as if all the three officers conspired together
to help the borrower, and it caused financial
loss  to  the  Corporation.   Therefore,  no
extraordinary  circumstances  exists  to  give
higher  and  shockingly  disproportionate
punishment to the appellant in W.A. No. 722/2009
while  giving  lesser  punishment  to  the  co-
delinquent.  This is nothing but treating the
equals  unequally.   This  aspect  were  not
considered  by  the  learned  Single  Judge.
Therefore, we are constrained to set aside the
order passed in W.P. No. 32090/2004.
XXX XXX XXX
21.  Even though such wide powers are conferred
on this Court to interfere with the punishment
and impose a lesser penalty and further the
punishment imposed on A. Mohan / the appellant
in  W.A.  No.  722/2009  is  also  shockingly
disproportionate to the proved delinquency, we
do not want to enter into the shoes of the
punishment imposing authority and we feel it
suffice  to  remit  the  matter  to  the  second
respondent with a direction to him to impose
just and appropriate punishment, proportionate
4

--- Page 23 ---
to  the  proved  delinquency,  on  A.  Mohan/the
appellant in W.A. No. 722/2009, keeping in view
our observations in this judgment and also the
punishment imposed on the co-delinquent.  The
second respondent is directed to complete the
entire exercise within a period of four weeks
from the date of receipt of a copy of this
judgment.”
8) Upon consideration of the facts of the present case,
we find that a common chargesheet was issued to all three
delinquent  employees,  and  the  allegations  levelled
against them are substantially similar in nature. After
inquiry, the Disciplinary Authority imposed penalty of
reduction in rank against A. Muruganantham, penalty of
removal from service against respondent no.1 – A. Mohan
(deceased) and penalty of reduction to a lower post on
respondent no.2 – G.K. Anbu. It is not in dispute that A.
Muruganantham  did  not  avail  any  further  remedy  by
preferring  an  appeal  against  the  order  of  such
punishment. However, the present respondents-employees,
A. Mohan (deceased) and G.K. Anbu, preferred appeals
before the Appellate Authority, which was of the view
that the penalty of removal and demotion, respectively,
is  inadequate.  Accordingly,  show  cause  notice  for
enhancement  of  the  punishment  was  issued  to  the
respondents-employees.  Thereafter, respondent no.1 – A.
5

--- Page 24 ---
Mohan (deceased) was saddled with the punishment of
dismissal, modifying the order of removal and respondent
no.2 – G.K. Anbu with the punishment of dismissal,
modifying the order of demotion.   
9) Both the respondents-employees assailed the order of
the Appellate Authority by filing Writ Petition No. 3273
of 2004 and 32090 of 2004 respectively before the High
Court. The learned Single Judge in the case of respondent
no.1 – A. Mohan (deceased) dismissed the writ petition,
while allowing the writ petition of respondent no.2 –
G.K. Anbu by setting aside the order of dismissal and
maintaining the order of demotion as passed by the
Disciplinary Authority. 
10) In consequence, respondent no.1 – A.Mohan (deceased)
and  the  appellant  no.1  –  employer  preferred  their
respective writ appeals, which have been decided vide the
impugned  judgment  by  remitting  the  matter  to  the
Appellate  Authority  on  the  issue  of  penalty,  in
particular, looking to the issue of discrimination and
differently dealing with the employees who were part of
the same enquiry based on common thread of allegations.
It is, inter alia, contended that there is no material
6

--- Page 25 ---
distinction in the imputation of allegations as indicated
in the chargesheet.  It is further urged that no material
distinction in the statements of the witnesses was found
insofar as the roles assigned to the individual employees
are concerned.  In the facts of the present case, it is
clear that the allegation of defalcation and breach of
trust against all three employees is similar. When such
is  the  case,  they  cannot  be  treated  differently
especially in light of the facts, pleadings and material
brought on record. The allegations against the employees
found place in the common chargesheet and the enquiry
also being common, it is merely after the enquiry report
that the Disciplinary Authority as well as the Appellate
Authority treated them separately, taking into account
the  degree  of  responsibility  associated  with  their
respective positions.
11) In addition, the distinction in treatment of the
employees appears to have arisen solely on account of the
respondents nos. 1 and 2, A. Mohan (deceased) and G.K.
Anbu, having exercised their right of appeal, while no
such  recourse  was  undertaken  in  the  case  of  A.
Muruganantham. 
7

--- Page 26 ---
12) After hearing the learned counsel, in our view, when
out  of  three  employees,  two  have  been  treated
differently,  despite  all  being  part  of  the  same
chargesheet in the departmental enquiry, the view taken
by the Division Bench of the High Court to remit the
matter back for consideration by the Appellate Authority,
is equitable and does not warrant any interference in the
peculiar facts of this case.
13) Accordingly, maintaining the order of the Division
Bench of the High Court, we dismiss the present appeals
and direct the Appellate Authority to take a final call
and decide the issue in view of the observations made
hereinabove within a period of three months from the date
of communication of this order.
14) Pending application(s), if any, shall stand disposed
of.
…………………………………………………………J.
[J.K. MAHESHWARI]
…………………………………………………………J.
[ALOK ARADHE]
NEW DELHI;
MAY 14, 2026.

9

--- Page 28 ---
IN THE SUPREME COURT OF INDIA
CIVIL APPELLATE JURISDICTION
CIVIL APPEAL NO.5168/2012
SIMLESH DEVI & ORS. APPELLANT(S)
                              VERSUS
THE COLLECTOR & ORS. RESPONDENT(S)
WITH
CIVIL APPEAL NO.5176/2012
CIVIL APPEAL NO.5175/2012
O R D E R
1. These three civil appeals arise out of the judgment
dated 04.09.2009 passed by a Division Bench of the
Allahabad High Court, whereby the acquisition of the land
situated at village Ibadullahpur @ Badalpur in District
Gautam Budh Nagar (formerly part of District Ghaziabad)
stood upheld and consequently the appellants’ prayer to
exempt their small residential plots/properties from the
acquisition has been rejected.
2. To recapitulate the facts briefly, the State of
Uttar Pradesh issued a notification on 20.06.2007 under
1

--- Page 29 ---
Section 4 of the Land Acquisition Act, 1894 (in short,
the  “Act”)  proposing  to  acquire  land  measuring
approximately  230  hectares  situated  at  village
Ibadullahpur @ Badalpur, Tehsil Dadri, Gautam Budh Nagar
for the public purpose of industrial development of
Greater Noida Development Authority. It was followed by a
notification dated 18.06.2008 issued under Section 6 of
the Act. It, however, seems that simultaneously, while
issuing notification under Section 4 of the Act, Section
17(1)  of  the  Act,  namely,  the  urgency  clause,  was
invoked. The State Government, in that regard, accepted
the recommendations of the District Collector on the
premise that the subject land was required urgently in
order to develop it as an industrial area and to invite
foreign investments.
3. So far as the appellants are concerned, they are
said to have purchased small plots measuring 100 sq. yds.
to 200 sq. yds., apparently for residential purposes in
the subject area, in and around the time the Section 4
notification was issued. It is also a matter of record
that, though no regulated development of a residential
colony  over  the  subject  land  was  approved  by  the
competent authority, the appellants or similarly placed
persons  are  said  to  have  constructed  their  small
2

--- Page 30 ---
residential units at their respective sites. It is for
this precise reason that in their writ petitions, the
appellants, instead of questioning the legality of the
grounds of urgency to justify the invocation of Section
17(1) of the Act, primarily sought the release of their
residential plots/dwelling units.
4. The appellants, being aggrieved by the acquisition,
approached the jurisdictional High Court through various
writ petitions in which initially ad interim protection
against dispossession was granted to them. Their writ
petitions,  however,  were  eventually  dismissed  vide
impugned judgment dated 04.09.2009. The acquisition as
well as the invocation of urgency under Section 17(1) of
the Act were upheld by the High Court and in para 25, it
opined as follows:
“25. From  a  bare  perusal  of  the  aforesaid
report of the committee, we find that the
proposal submitted by the committee was duly
countersigned by the Collector, Gautam Budh
Nagar. The said report clearly recites the
urgency for which the land was required, namely
to  provide  land  to  prospective  potential
investors  including  foreign  investors  to
support the planned industrial development in
the State of U.P. The proposal, as noted above,
also recites that in the event such land is not
provided immediately, then the said investors
would  migrate  to  other  States  which  would
definitely  have  an  adverse  impact  on  the
planned industrial development of the State. It
is only when that such investors are provided
immediate  allotments  that  such  planned
3

--- Page 31 ---
industrial development would be possible. It
is, thus, for the said public purpose coupled
with the aforesaid urgency, the proposal was
made for invoking the provisions of Section 17
of the Act. The Certificate issued by the
Collector after receiving of the said report
also reemphasis the same and clearly spells out
the need to dispense 'with the inquiry under
Section 5-A .of 'the Act'. It is this material,
which was there before the State Government
which prompted it to invoke the urgency clause
not only under Section 17(1) but also under
sub-section (4) of Section 17 of 'the Act'.
Thus, on the facts of the present case, it
cannot be said that there was no material
before the State Government for invoking the
urgency clause.”
[Sic]
5. The aggrieved appellants thereafter approached this
Court. When the matter came up for hearing on 26.07.2010,
status quo  was directed to be maintained till further
orders. That interim protection has continued to operate
for almost 16 years.
6. We have heard learned counsel for the appellants as
well as Mr. Ravindra Kumar, learned Senior Counsel for
Greater Noida and learned State counsel for the State of
Uttar Pradesh.
7. It is vehemently urged on behalf of the respondents
that the urgency clause was invoked for bona fide reasons
to facilitate foreign investment in the fast-developing
cosmopolitan area of Noida/Greater Noida, where several
4

--- Page 32 ---
residential, commercial, industrial, and institutional
activities have already been developed. It is, thus,
urged that the reasons assigned by the High Court for
upholding  the  urgency  clause  do  not  call  for  any
interference by this Court.
8. On  the  other  hand,  lear ned  counsel  for  the
appellants submits that they are not keen on challenging
the acquisition in its entirety as their only endeavour
is to save their residential units, especially since they
do not belong to affluent sections of the society, have
poured their life’s savings into their homes, and do not
have any other alternate form of social security.
9. We have given thoughtful consideration to the rival
submissions.
10. In view of the fact that all 16 appellants in these
three appeals have approached this Court, primarily for
the protection of their residential units admeasuring 100
sq. yds to 200 sq. yds. and have not seriously agitated
the issue of quashing the entire acquisition, we are
satisfied that there is no necessity for this Court to
revisit the grounds of invoking the urgency clause. The
short issue that survives for consideration is whether,
notwithstanding that the subject acquisition has been
5

--- Page 33 ---
held to be valid and in accordance with law, the dwelling
units  of  the  appellants  should  be  exempted  from
acquisition. In this regard, we find that the process for
the subject acquisition commenced in June 2007, i.e.
almost 19 years ago. The appellants’ possession has been
protected by the Courts throughout. It also appears from
the counter affidavits/affidavits filed by the Greater
Noida  Authorities  that  residential  units  have  been
constructed,  though  the  same  may  be  unauthorized.
Regulated development of the rest of the area has also
apparently taken place.
11. In these peculiar facts and circumstances, we find
it a fit case to invoke our powers under Article 142 of
the Constitution of India to do complete justice between
the parties and consequently allow these appeals in part
in the following terms:
(i) The subject acquisition qua the residential plots of
the appellants in these three appeals is set aside,
without affecting the acquisition of the rest of the
land.
(ii) Consequently,  the  residential  houses  of  the
appellants shall remain exempt from the acquisition.
(iii) The appellants, whose residential houses have been
exempted from acquisition, may apply for the grant of
basic amenities by the Authority. However, in that event,
6

--- Page 34 ---
they  shall  be  liable  to  deposit  the  prescribed
development charges as may be determined by the Authority
as per the regulations.
 
..........................CJI.
(SURYA KANT)
............................J.  
(V. MOHANA)  
NEW DELHI;        
June 17, 2026

--- Page 35 ---

--- Page 68 ---
IN THE SUPREME COURT OF INDIA
CIVIL APPELLATE JURISDICTION
CIVIL APPEAL NOS.8254-8255 of 2013
M/S SUN PHARMACEUTICALS
INDUSTRIES LTD. … APPELLANT
VERSUS
M/S WEST COAST PHARMACEUTICAL
WORK LD & ANR.    … RESPONDENTS
O R D E R
1. The  appellant  has  preferred  the  present  appeals
challenging the final judgment and order dated 20.06.2012
passed by the High Court of Gujarat at Ahmedabad, which had
dismissed its Appeal From Order No.29 of 2012 arising from
the order dated 23.01.2012 passed by the learned Chamber
Judge,  City  Civil  Court,  Ahmedabad,  dismissing  the
temporary injunction application filed by the appellant and
vacating the ad-interim order granted earlier in the said
matter.
2. The appellant had filed a suit for passing off action
and  for  restraining  the  respondents  from  using  the
trademark “ACICAL”. The appellant was manufacturing and
marketing and selling a product “ACUCAL” and it had applied
1

--- Page 69 ---
for registration which was pending consideration when the
suit was filed.  It was the case of the appellant that the
usage  of  the  word  “ACICAL”  by  the  respondents  is
deceptively similar to their product “ACUCAL” and the
appellant had applied for cease-and-desist order before the
trial court.  Though the trial court had granted an ex-
parte injunction at the ad-interim stage, after notice and
after hearing the parties the trial court dismissed the
injunction application holding that the medical products of
both  the  parties  operated  in  different  areas  and,
therefore, the plaintiff is not entitled to an injunction.
The trial court also noticed that the trademark “ACUCAL”
had still not been registered and, therefore, the appellant
is not entitled for any discretionary relief and that it
has failed to prove that there is deceptive similarity
between  trademark  “ACUCAL”  and  “ACICAL”  which  creates
confusion amongst doctors, chemist, traders or public in
general, thereby dismissing the notice of motion.
3. The appellant filed an appeal before the High Court
of  Gujarat  at  Ahmedabad.  Before  the  High  Court,  the
appellant had also relied upon a judgment of this Court in
Cadila Health Care Ltd. V. Cadila Pharmaceuticals Ltd.
reported in (2001) 5 SCC 73.  The High Court, while
distinguishing the judgment passed in Cadila Health Care
(supra), upheld the order of the trial court and dismissed
2

--- Page 70 ---
the appeal. The appellant challenged the said order of the
High  Court  and  notice  was  issued  by  this  Court  on
06.08.2012. On 12.09.2013, this Court, after noticing the
judgment in Cadila Health Care Ltd.  (supra), had granted
leave in the matter and stayed the operation of the
impugned order during the pendency of the appeal.
4. It appears during the pendency of the appeal in this
Court,  the appellant herein has obtained the registration
for the trademark “ACUCAL”.  Subsequently,  the parties
seem to have entered into the Settlement Agreement on
11.10.2024, by virtue of which the appellant and the
respondents have come to an agreement that the respondents
will  cease  and  desist  from  dealing  in  the  medical
preparations under the impugned trademark “ACICAL” and any
of  its  extensions  or  any  other  marks  which  may  be
deceptively similar to the appellant’s registered trademark
“ACUCAL”.  The respondents have also agreed to cease and
desist from using the trademark “ACUCAL” and that they will
abandon their application for the trademark “ACICAL”.  The
parties have agreed that the order dated 23.01.2012 passed
by the City Civil Court, Ahmedabad, Gujarat in Civil Suit
No.  2800/2011  as  well  as  the  impugned  order  dated
20.06.2012 passed by the High Court Gujarat be set aside
and  that  the  parties  shall  be  making  an  appropriate
application for the same.
3

--- Page 71 ---
5. On  the  basis  of  this  settlement  agreement,
application dated 14.10.2024 being I.A. No.23575 of 2024
has been filed before this Court seeking disposal of the
present appeals in terms of the settlement arrived at
between the parties.
6. This Court has perused the Settlement Agreement and
heard the appellant.  Today when the matter was taken up
for  hearing,  neither  the  respondents  nor  their
representatives were present. The counsel for the appellant
represented at the Bar, that the respondents have signed
the  agreement  with  full  authority  through  proper
representations and the settlement have been effected.
7. Heard the appellant and perused the application and
the enclosed Settlement Agreement along with the authority
letters executed by the parties.
8. In view of the settlement and the terms agreed
thereunder these appeals are allowed. The order dated
23.01.2012, passed by the Ld. Trial Court in Notice of
Motion Exhs. 6/7 and 16 in Civil Suit No.2800/20121 before
the City Civil Court, Ahmedabad, Gujarat, as well as the
4

--- Page 72 ---
order dated 20.06.2012 by the High Court of Gujarat in
Appeal No.29 of 2012, are set aside in the light of the
settlement reached between the parties.  The Settlement
Agreement is taken on record and it will form part of this
order.
9. Since the respondents were not present today, it is
open to the respondents to approach this Court in case if
they have an objection to the recording of the settlement
and the disposal of the appeals in terms of the settlement,
within a period of four months from today.
10. The appeals are disposed of accordingly.
 …………………………………,CJI.
  [SURYA KANT]
 ………………………………………,J.
     [V. MOHANA]
NEW DELHI;
JUNE 17, 2026.

          UPON hearing the counsel the Court made the following
                             O R D E R
1. We have heard learned counsel for the applicant
Shaik  Rahamthulla  and  learned  counsel  for  the
respondent-State of Andhra Pradesh.
2. Interlocutory Application No.179485/2026 has been
filed by the applicant in Criminal Appeal No.3128/2025
whereas Interlocutory Application No.179505/2026 has
been  filed  by  the  applicant  in  Criminal  Appeal
No.3127/2025. In both the Criminal Appeals, applicant
is the appellant.
3. Appellant has been convicted by the Sessions Court
under Section 396 read with 120B and Section 400 of the
Indian Penal Code, 1860 (IPC) and sentenced to undergo
Rigorous Imprisonment (R.I.) for life amongst others.
Appeal filed by the applicant before the High Court was
dismissed  where  after,  the  related  Special  Leave
Petitions were filed before this Court and on leave
being granted, those have been registered as Criminal
Appeals.  In  the  two  Interlocutory  applications,
applicant has stated that he is aged about 75 years and
has  severe  cardiac  issues.  The  condition  of  the
appellant is stated in Paragraph 9 of Interlocutory
Application No.179485/2026 which reads as under:
“That the applicant/appellant is an old
2

--- Page 82 ---
man, aged 75 years. He is a known case of
Chronic  Rheumatic  Heart  Disease  (CRHD)
with  Severe  Calcific  MS  tissue.  CRHD
involves heavy, rigid calcium deposits on
the  mitral valve  apparatus. While  CRHD
usually  causes  commissural  fusion,  the
added severe calcification makes the valve
leaflets non-pliable and increases risks
during intervention. Owing to his severe
heart condition, the applicant/appellant
had to undergo Mitral Valve Replacement
with 27mm CE Paramount Tissue Valve. The
applicant/appellant is also a patient of
Diabetes and Hypertension and suffers from
cataract and dribbling of urine.”
4. On 18.06.2026, we had called upon Ms. Prerna
Singh, learned counsel for the respondent-State of
Andhra Pradesh to obtain instructions and to submit a
medical report on the next date, i.e. today.
5. Today, learned counsel for the respondent-State
had produced the medical report along with the covering
letter of the Superintendent of Jails, Central Jail,
Nellore dated 20.06.2026.
6. That  apart,  the  Director  of  Sri  Venkateswara
Institute of Medical Sciences (SVIMS) has sent an email
stating the following:
“1. This procedure is available at SVIMS.
3

--- Page 83 ---
2. The estimated cost of the procedure is
approximately 20 lakhs. The required funds will₹
need to be arranged.
3. Not all patients are suitable candidates
for this procedure.
4. A  detailed  evaluation  is  necessary  to
determine whether it is appropriate for him.
5. Kindly send him to SVIMS for evaluation.
The assessment process requires approximately
one week of hospitalization.”
7. Further, we have seen from the medical report that
the  applicant  has  undergone  several  rounds  of
hospitalizations at Nellore as well as at Tirupati.
8. Learned counsel for the respondent-State fairly
submits that the Court may consider granting bail to
the applicant on medical ground for a limited period.
9. On a query by the Court, learned counsel for the
applicant submits that his family is willing to support
his medical treatment and the expenses that may be
incurred in such treatment and that he would be looked
after during his medical treatment.
10. Considering the advanced age of the applicant and
his medical condition, we grant medical bail to the
applicant Shaik Rahamthulla for a period of three
months from the date of his release.
11. Accordingly, we direct that the applicant shall be
produced before the concerned Trial Court within a
4

--- Page 84 ---
maximum period of seven days from today, where after
the Trial Court shall release the applicant on bail on
such terms and conditions as may be deemed fit and
proper.
12. Interlocutory  Application  No.179485/2026  in
Criminal  Appeal  No.3128/2025  and  Interlocutory
Application  No.179505/2026  in  Criminal  Appeal
No.3127/2025 are accordingly disposed of.
13. List in due course.
(ABHINAV KUMAR)                                 (SAPNA BANSAL)

IN THE SUPREME COURT OF INDIA
CRIMINAL APPELLATE JURISDICTION
CRIMINAL APPEAL NO(S).          OF 2026
(@ SPECIAL LEAVE PETITION (CRL.) NO(S).8830 OF 2026)
SANJAY VERMA                               APPELLANT

THE STATE OF JHARKHAND                    RESPONDENT
O R D E R
Leave granted.
This appeal challenges the judgment and order
dated 08.04.2026 passed by the High Court of
Jharkhand at Ranchi, in B.A.NO.2738/2026.
The appellant herein has been booked for the
crime registered pursuant to FIR NO.237/2025
dated  26.07.2025  lodged  with  Balidih  Police
Station,  District  Bokaro,  with  respect  to
offences punishable under Sections 331(4) and
305(a) of the Bharatiya Nyaya Sanhita, 2023
(“BNS”).
An application seeking regular bail having
1

--- Page 86 ---
been rejected by the High Court  vide  impugned
order  dated  08.04.2026,  the  appellant  has
preferred the instant appeal. 
This Court vide its order dated 18.05.2026,
issued notice in the instant matter.
Heard learned counsel for the appellant in
support of the appeal and learned counsel for
the respondent-State and perused the material on
record. 
Learned counsel for the appellant submitted
that the appellant had no knowledge of the fact
that  he  was  purchasing  stolen  jewellery.
Although the recovery may have been made from
him the fact remains that he is a  bona fide
purchaser. Nevertheless, he has been in jail
since 28.12.2025 and since the charges have
already  been  framed  and  there  are  seven
witnesses to be examined, the relief of bail may
be granted to the appellant herein by setting
aside the impugned order.
Per  contra ,  learned  counsel  for  the
2

--- Page 87 ---
respondent-State with reference to the counter
affidavit contended that since the recovery of
the jewellery has been made from the appellant
herein, there is a strong case for conviction
and in the circumstances, it was submitted that
there is no merit in this appeal.
Considering the facts on record, in our view,
the case for bail is made out.
We, therefore, allow this appeal and direct
as under:
“The appellant shall be produced before
the  concerned  Trial  Court  as  early  as
possible and the Trial Court shall release
him on bail, subject to such conditions as
it may deem appropriate to impose to ensure
his presence in the proceedings arising out
of FIR No.237/2025 mentioned above.”
It  is  directed  that  the  appellant  shall
extend complete cooperation in the trial of the
instant case. 
The appellant shall not misuse his liberty in
any manner.
3

--- Page 88 ---
Any infraction of the conditions may entail
in cancellation of the bail granted to the
appellant.
With  these  observations,  the  appeal  is
allowed.

1. We have heard learned counsel for the petitioner,
Deputy Director of Education, Nashik Division, State of
Maharashtra.
2. Delay condoned.
3. Relevant  portion  of  the  impugned  order  dated
12.02.2026 reads as under:
1

--- Page 96 ---
“14. If, in future, it is noticed that
their appointments were illegal and action
is  taken  against  them,  the  payment  of
further salaries shall depend on the action
so taken on that particular day, which
shall remain subject to judicial scrutiny.
15. In so far as the remaining outstanding
amounts are concerned, we direct that the
Headmaster  of  the  School  shall  submit
proper bills to the Education Officer, for
both, the arrears and the regular monthly
payments.
16.  The  learned  Additional  Government
Pleader  has  calculated  the  outstanding
amount towards salaries at Rs. 30,00,895/-
for  the  period  from  01.09.2016  to
30.09.2024, and Rs. 1,91,68,424/- for the
period from 01.09.2016 to 31.10.2024, which
shall be processed after the bills are
received  from  the  Management.  The
Management would also supply the requisite
documents.  We,  therefore,  direct  the
Management  to  comply  with  these
requirements  without  any  reservation  or
reluctance. We make it clear that if the
Management  displays  any  reluctance  in
producing  the  original  documents,  the
Education Department shall initiate steps
for appointment of an Administrator over
2

--- Page 97 ---
the Management.”
4. The Writ Petition was disposed of by the High
Court but respondents therein (petitioners herein) were
directed to submit compliance report on 27.03.2026.
There is nothing on record to show that compliance has
been submitted by the petitioners.
5. Learned Senior counsel for the petitioners submits
that though the appointment of the respondents are
highly questionable, nonetheless in terms of the order
of the High Court, the present salary has been paid.
Problem is relating to arrears of salary.
6. If the present salary has been paid, we fail to
understand as to how there can be any impediment to the
release of arrears of salary.
7. Moreover, there is nothing on record to show that
these appointments are illegal in nature.
8. At this stage, learned Senior Counsel for the
petitioners submits that enquiry is still going on.
9. Depending upon the outcome of the enquiry, it is
always open to the petitioners to take appropriate
action in accordance with law but till such time, as
directed by the High Court, the salary of the teachers
would have to be paid.
10. Though  tempted,  we  refrain  from  making  any
observations, at this stage, to the effect that if the
appointments were illegally made by the management, the
3

--- Page 98 ---
State would be at liberty to take action against the
managements for resorting to such illegal appointments,
including recovery of the salary amount.
11. We, therefore, do not find any good ground to
entertain the Special Leave Petition.
12. The same is, accordingly, dismissed.
13. Pending  application(s),  if  any,  shall  stand
disposed of.

CIVIL APPELLATE JURISDICTION
CIVIL APPEAL NO. 5977 OF 2014
DEFENCE ESTATE OFFICER PATHANKOT 
CIRCLE PATHANKOT & ANR.
APPELLANT(S)
VERSUS
JUGAL KISHORE S/O BELI RAM & ANR. RESPONDENT(S)
W I T H
CIVIL APPEAL NO.         OF 2026
(ARISING OUT OF SLP (CIVIL) NO. 7094 OF 2016)
O R D E R
1. Delay condoned.
2. Leave granted.
3. These appeals have been preferred by the Defence Estate
Officer, Pathankot Circle, Pathankot and other authorities and the
Union of India challenging the judgment dated 19.11.2013 passed by
the  High  Court  of  Punjab  and  Haryana  in  terms  whereof  the
respondent(s) have been held entitled to enhanced compensation at
par  with  their  co-owners,  regardless  of  the  fact  that  the
respondent(s) did not file any Reference Petition under Section 18
of the Land Acquisition Act, 1894.  
4. In the peculiar facts and circumstances of this case, we are
not inclined to interfere with the impugned judgment of the High
Court.  Consequently, let the respondent(s) also be paid the same
amount of compensation as has been paid to their co-sharers. The
due amount shall be deposited, if it is not already deposited, with
the Reference Court within six weeks, and the same shall be
1

--- Page 120 ---
disbursed to the respondent(s) along with interest as may be
assessed in accordance with law.
5. The appeals stand disposed of.

       (SURYA KANT)
..........................J.
       (V. MOHANA)

1. We have heard learned counsel for the parties.
2. Delay condoned.
3. Petitioner seeks transfer of divorce proceedings in
Marriage Petition No. HMA 3644 of 2024 titled as “Krishan
Kumar versus Kusum Saini” pending before the Principal
Judge, Family Court, (South-West), Dwarka Court, Delhi to
a competent Court in the District of Mathura, Uttar
Pradesh.
4. On 20.08.2025, this Court had issued notice and stayed
further proceedings at the Dwarka Court, Delhi.
5. Thereafter,  both  the  parties  were  referred  to
Mediation by this Court vide order dated 12.02.2026.
However, as per the mediation report dated 07.04.2026,
mediation has failed.
6. After hearing learned counsel for the parties and
going through the materials on record, we are of the view
that a case for transfer has been made out.
7. Accordingly, we direct that the entire case record of
Marriage Petition No. HMA 3644 of 2024 titled as “Krishan
1

--- Page 124 ---
Kumar versus Kusum Saini” pending before the Principal
Judge, Family Court, (South-West), Dwarka Court, Delhi be
transferred  to  the  Principal  Judge,  Family  Court  at
Mathura, Uttar Pradesh.
8. We also permit the respondent-husband to appear in the
proceedings  at  Mathura,  Uttar  Pradesh  through  Video
Conferencing, except on those days when his physical
appearance  is  considered  necessary  by  the  Transferee
Court.
9. We have been informed at the Bar that both the parties
have again approached the Mediation Centre at Mathura,
Uttar Pradesh.
10. If that be the case, then the Mediation Centre at
Mathura shall do the needful to explore the possibility of
a mediated settlement between the parties.

terms.

1. Leave granted.
2. The appellant was convicted for committing offence
under Section 138 of the Negotiable Instruments Act,
1881 and has been sentenced to pay fine/compensation of
Rs.6,50,000/- and litigation expenses of Rs.50,000/- to
the respondent/complainant.
3. The conviction was maintained by the Appellate
Court and the High Court as well in the Revision
Petition under the impugned order. Subsequent thereto,
the  appellant  has  paid  the  entire  amount  to  the
complainant as is evident from the application and
affidavit filed by the complainant before the Chief
Judicial Magistrate, Nagaon (Assam).
4. It is stated in the application that the appellant
is serving the sentence since 23.02.2026. It is also
1

--- Page 128 ---
stated in the application that the appellant is an old
age sick man, hence the complainant has compromised this
case with the accused/appellant outside the Court by
receiving Rs.7,00,000/-.
5. In view of the above, since the complainant has
compromised with the appellant after accepting the full
amount of compensation and litigation expenses amounting
to Rs.7,00,000/-, we record the compromise and set aside
the impugned order of conviction.
6. The appellant be released from jail forthwith,
unless he is required in any other case.
7. The Appeal is disposed of in the above terms.

disposed of.

IN THE SUPREME COURT OF INDIA
CRIMINAL APPELLATE JURISDICTION
CRIMINAL APPEAL NO. 3084 OF 2026
(@ SPECIAL LEAVE PETITION (CRIMINAL) NO.8416/2026)
JETIN @ JATIL ASHOK SATDIVE     APPELLANT(S)
VERSUS
THE STATE OF MAHARASHTRA         RESPONDENT(S)
ORDER
1.  We have heard learned counsel for the appellant and
learned counsel for the respondent-State of Maharashtra.
2.  Leave granted.
3. This Appeal is directed against the order dated
06.02.2026 passed by the High Court of Judicature at
Bombay, Bench at Aurangabad (‘High Court’ in short) in
Bail Application No.2188 of 2025, rejecting the bail
prayer of the appellant.
4. Appellant  is  an  accused  in  FIR  No.310  of  2023
registered  at  Police  Station-  Kopargaon,  District-
Ahmednagar charged under Sections 302, 207/34 of the
Indian Penal Code, 1860 (IPC). The appellant was arrested
on 01.07.2023.
5. This Court, vide order dated 13.05.2026 had issued
1

--- Page 136 ---
notice. Thereafter, leaned counsel for the respondent-
State of Maharashtra has filed counter affidavit.
6. Learned  counsel  for  the  respondent-State  of
Maharashtra has drawn the attention of the Court to
Paragraph 15 of the counter affidavit to submit that on
the same day, appellant was involved in another criminal
case registered under Section 307 IPC. Further, in the
present case, there are eye witnesses who have clearly
identified the appellant as one of the assailants who had
stabbed the victim.
7. Learned counsel for the appellant submits that in so
far the other case, being CR No.312 of 2023, is concerned,
the appellant has been granted bail by the Trial Court on
19.10.2023. As regards the present case is concerned,
learned counsel submits that appellant is in custody for
more than three years. Though charge sheet was submitted
way  back  in  the  year  2024,  the  trial  has  not  yet
commenced.  Prosecution  has  cited  37  witnesses.  The
completion of the trial is realistically not possible in
the near future.
8. Having regard to the above and taking an overall view
of the matter, we are of the opinion that a case for bail
is made out.
9. Accordingly, we direct that the appellant shall be
produced before the concerned Trial Court within a maximum
period of seven days from today, where after the Trial
Court shall release the appellant on bail on such terms
2

--- Page 137 ---
and conditions as may be deemed fit and proper.
10. The Appeal is accordingly allowed in the aforesaid
terms.
11. Pending application(s), if any, shall stand disposed
of.

    IN THE SUPREME COURT OF INDIA
CRIMINAL APPELLATE JURISDICTION
CRIMINAL APPEAL NO.  3075­3076 OF 2026 
(Arising out of SLP (Crl.) No.2802­2803 of 2025)
JAGDISH PARSHAD PANWAR                             Appellant(s)
                                VERSUS
UJWAL @ JAGDISH & ANR. ETC.                        Respondent(s)
O R D E R
1.  Leave granted.
2.  We   have   heard   the   learned   counsel   appearing   for   the
parties.
3.  The respondents were charged for the offences punishable
under Sections 302, 326, and 120B r/w Section 34 of the Indian
Penal Code, 1860 and Section 25(1)(a) of the Arms Act, 1959,
inter alia, alleging that they, along with the co­accused,
hatched a plan to kill the deceased. An application seeking
discharge was filed before the Trial Court. The Trial Court
dismissed the discharge application by taking note of not only
the offences involved, but also the materials available on
record. The High Court, vide the impugned order, has discharged

--- Page 140 ---
2
the respondents in exercise of its revisional jurisdiction.
Aggrieved, the present appeals have been filed.
4. We find force in the submission of the learned counsel
appearing for the appellant that the High Court has conducted a
mini­trial,   while   exercising   revisional   jurisdiction,   and
discharged the respondents.
5. We are dealing with a charge which is punishable with
imprisonment for life. Suffice it is to state that the impugned
order passed by the High Court cannot be sustained in the eye of
the law. Accordingly, the same is set aside.
6. Consequently, the appeals stand allowed.
7. Pending application(s), if any, shall stand disposed of.

          UPON hearing the counsel the Court made the following
                             O R D E R
1. Upon hearing learned counsel for the parties, we are
prima facie of the view that the petitioner was wrongly
denied participation in the stray round.
2. Had she been allowed to participate, the subject PG
Seat in M.S. Obstetrics-Gynecology under the NRI quota in
Maharishi Markandeshwar College of Medical Science and
Research,  Sadopur,  Ambala  would  have  gone  to  the
petitioner,  however,  the  said  seat  was  allotted  to
respondent No. 6 under the order of the High Court in the
impugned order.
3. Learned counsel for the respondent Nos. 3 and 4 has
produced before us a chart showing vacancy position in

IN THE SUPREME COURT OF INDIA
CIVIL APPELLATE JURISDICTION
MISCELLANEOUS APPLICATION DIARY NO. 37939 OF 2026
IN
(CIVIL APPEAL NO. 8466 of 2026)
ABHISHEK BANERJEE  APPELLANT(S)
VERSUS
M/S. EMTA COAL LIMITED & ANR. RESPONDENT(S)
O R D E R
1. Upon mentioning it is brought to our notice that
there are some inadvertent errors in paragraph Nos.3, 4
and 5 of the order passed by this Court on 12.06.2026 in
Civil Appeal No. 8466 of 2026.
2. Considering  the  submissions,  we  substitute  the
existing paragraph Nos.3, 4 and 5 of the order in the
following manner:
“3. Having gone through the judgment, we
are of the view that it is a well reasoned
order,  therefore,  it  does  not  warrant
interference. It is contended that the impugned
order may lead to unwarranted refunds to the
respondent(s)-company, based on the Calcutta
High Court judgment in Commissioner of Service
Tax, Kolkata vs. Electrosteel Castings Limited1
therefore, if the law is not settled by this
Court,  similar  parties  would  approach  the
authorities  including  CESTAT  for  seeking
similar relief.
1   2025 (393) E.L.T 36 (Cal.)

--- Page 159 ---
4. If  the  law  has  been  settled  by  some
decision of the High Court, it remains binding
till it is set aside or overruled by the
Supreme Court, and the Tribunal or authorities
cannot ignore the judgment of the High Court.
Till it is set aside or overruled, the same
would  hold  the  field  and  the  Tribunal  or
authorities would not commit any error of law
by relying upon judgment of the Calcutta High
Court.
5. It is also to be noticed that the law has
been settled by the Supreme Court also in Civil
Appeal (Diary) No. 33259 of 2018 by order dated
05.10.2018 against an earlier order of the
similar nature in the matter of Marmugao Port
Trust  vs.  Commissioner  of  Customs,  Central
Excise  & Service Tax 2, which has been relied
upon by the Tribunal.”
3.  In view of the above, the miscellaneous application
is disposed of.

PRIYANK KUMAR UPADHYAY @

VERSUS
THE STATE OF BIHAR         RESPONDENT(S)
ORDER
1.  We have heard learned counsel for the appellant(s) and
learned counsel for the respondent State of Bihar.
2.  Leave granted.
3. Despite opportunity being granted, learned counsel
for the respondent-State of Bihar has not filed counter
affidavit. We, therefore, propose to proceed with the
hearing of this case.
4. Appellant(s) seek regular bail in connection with FIR
No.06/2026 registered at Police Station- Sikrol, District-
Buxar, Bihar for the offence punishable under Sections
191(2), 191(3), 126(2), 115(2), 109, 50, 61(2), 103(1),
351(2) and 352 of the Bharatiya Nyaya Sanhita, 2023 and
Section 27 of the Arms Act, 1959.
5. As per the case of the prosecution, one Kanhaiya
Chaubey and others had gone to harvest the agricultural
field forcibly and in that process, had fired from a fire
1

--- Page 165 ---
arm leading to the death of the deceased. Allegation is
that present appellant(s) were also part of the group
which had gone to the agricultural field and had assaulted
the deceased and four other persons.
6. Appellant(s)  are  in  custody  since  08.01.2026.
Investigation is complete and charge sheet has been filed.
Though prosecution has cited six witnesses, none has been
examined till date.
7. Learned counsel for the appellant(s) submits that a
co-accused has been granted bail by the High Court.
8. Having regard to the above and on due consideration,
we are of the view that a case for bail is made out.
9. Accordingly, we direct that the appellant(s) shall be
produced before the concerned Trial Court within a maximum
period of seven days from today, where after the Trial
Court shall release the appellant(s) on bail on such terms
and conditions as may be deemed fit and proper.
10. The Appeal is, accordingly, allowed.
11. Pending application(s), if any, shall stand disposed
of.

For Respondent(s) : 
   UPON hearing the counsel the Court made the following
                             O R D E R
1. We have heard learned counsel for petitioner No.1/wife.
2. In a petition filed by petitioner No.1/wife under Section 12
of the Protection of Women From Domestic Violence Act, 2005, the
learned Magistrate, vide order dated 28.01.2025, had, inter alia,
directed  respondent  No.2/husband  that  he  should  allow  the
complainant (petitioner No.1/wife) and her daughter to reside
peacefully in one part of the shared residence.
1

--- Page 168 ---
3. The  appeal  filed  by  respondent  No.2/husband  against  the
aforesaid order was dismissed by the learned Sessions Judge,
Hamirpur, whereafter respondent No.2/husband preferred a criminal
revision petition before the High Court of Judicature at Allahabad
(briefly  ‘the  High  Court’  hereinafter).  While  dismissing  the
criminal revision petition  vide the impugned judgment and order
dated 09.03.2026, the High Court directed as follows:
“9. The maintenance awarded by the trial court of
Rs. 5,000/- per month in total in favour of
opposite party nos. 2 and 3 cannot be said to be
excessive, rather it is already on the lower
side. Therefore, the impugned order passed by the
trial court does not warrant any interference by
this Court.
10. The revisionist is directed to provide rental
accommodation of Rs.5,000/- per month to opposite
party nos. 2 and 3 as per their choice.”
4. Learned counsel for petitioner No.1/wife has made a grievance
that since there is no mention in the impugned judgment and order
of the High Court about the order passed by the learned Magistrate
qua the shared residence, it may be construed that the direction to
the  revisionist  (respondent  No.2/husband)  to  provide  rental
accommodation would mean that petitioner No.1/wife should vacate
the shared residence.
5. In the circumstances, we are, prima facie, of the view that
when the High Court has dismissed the revision petition of the
respondent No.2/husband, the order passed by the learned Magistrate
on 28.01.2025 including the residence order would continue to hold
the field.
6. Issue notice, returnable on 11.08.2026.
2

--- Page 169 ---
7. In the meanwhile, the operation of paragraph No.10 of the
impugned judgment and order of the High Court dated 09.03.2026
shall remain stayed until further orders.
       (SOURAV PAL)                              (SAPNA BANSAL)
SENIOR PERSONAL ASSISTANT                     COURT MASTER (NSH)

RAMBALI RAI & ORS.                                 PETITIONER(S)
                                VERSUS
THE STATE OF BIHAR                                 RESPONDENT(S)
IA No. 181414/2026 - EXEMPTION FROM FILING C/C OF THE IMPUGNED 
JUDGMENT
IA No. 181415/2026 - EXEMPTION FROM FILING O.T.
 
Date : 24-06-2026 This matter was called on for hearing today.
CORAM : 
         HON'BLE MR. JUSTICE UJJAL BHUYAN
         HON'BLE MR. JUSTICE ARUN PALLI
[PARTIAL COURT WORKING DAYS BENCH]
For Petitioner(s) :Mr. Raja Choudhary, Adv.
                   Ms. Anushika Mishra, Adv.
                   Mr. Rajesh Singh Chauhan, AOR                   
                   
For Respondent(s) :Mr. Azmat H. Amanullah, AOR
    Ms. Vanshita Gupta, Adv. 
        UPON hearing the counsel the Court made the following
                             O R D E R
1. We have heard learned counsel for the petitioners and also
learned counsel for the respondent/the State of Bihar.
2. Learned counsel for the petitioners seeks anticipatory bail in
connection with Desari Police Station Case No.676 of 2024 dated
29.07.2024 registered under Section 80 read with Section 3(5) of
the Bharatiya Nyaya Sanhita, 2023.
3. Petitioners are the immediate family members of the husband
1

--- Page 171 ---
whose wife had died at her matrimonial home on 27.07.2024 under
unnatural circumstances. As per the post-mortem report, the cause
of death is shown as “Asphyxia due to Hanging”.
4. Learned counsel for the petitioners submits that husband was
given the benefit of default bail. Besides, other family members of
the husband have also been granted anticipatory bail by the High
Court.
5. Therefore, petitioners should be granted the benefit of pre-
arrest bail by this Court.
6. Learned counsel for the respondent/State, on the other hand,
points out that the incident had happened on 27.07.2024 and the
case was registered in July, 2024. Till now, the petitioners, who
are immediate family members of the husband, have managed to remain
at large. She submits that those who have been granted anticipatory
bail by the High Court are not the immediate family members of the
husband.
7. We find that though the FIR was registered way back in July,
2024, till date petitioners have not been summoned by the police of
Desari Police Station. Further, we find that because of lack of any
progress in the investigation, the husband was granted the benefit
of default bail by the Court. Such conduct on the part of the
Investigating Authority cannot be appreciated. That apart, in a
case  relating  to  dowry  death,  question  of  granting
anticipatory/pre-arrest bail to the husband or to the immediate
family members, who resided in the matrimonial home where the
incident had occurred, does not arise.
8. At  this  stage,  we  may  also  mention  that  the  initial
2

--- Page 172 ---
anticipatory bail application filed by the petitioners, being
Criminal Misc. No.13340 of 2025, was dismissed by the High Court on
30.10.2025. Even thereafter, the police has not deemed it fit to
summon the petitioners for investigation.
9. This speaks volumes about the conduct of the police in
carrying out the investigation.
10. In such circumstances, no case for anticipatory bail is made
out.
11. The special leave is, accordingly, dismissed.
12. Pending application(s), if any, shall stand disposed of. 
       (SOURAV PAL)                              (SAPNA BANSAL)
SENIOR PERSONAL ASSISTANT                     COURT MASTER (NSH)
3

--- Page 173 ---

1

--- Page 174 ---
by  the  Trial  Court  with  permanent  alimony  of
Rs.20,00,000/-. Appeal filed by the petitioner-husband
before the High Court came to be rejected.
4. Learned counsel for the petitioner-husband has
drawn the attention of the Court to Paragraph 52 of the
Special Leave Petition Paper Book to contend that
respondent-wife had agreed to withdraw the other cases
pending between the parties, i.e. under the Domestic
Violence Act, 2005 and a criminal case registered under
Section 498A of the Indian Penal Code, 1860.
5. However,  we  do  not  find  any  such  concession
recorded either by the courts below or in any evidence
to that effect. If at all such a concession has been
given by the respondent-wife in some other proceeding,
it would be open to the petitioner to seek closure of
such proceeding on the basis of such concession but
that cannot be a ground to reopen the concurrent
findings of the courts below in so far the present
Special Leave Petition is concerned.
6. Subject to the above, the Special Leave Petition
is dismissed.
7. Pending  application(s),  if  any,  shall  stand
disposed of.

1. We have heard Mr. S. Nagamuthu, learned Senior
counsel for the petitioner(s) and Mr. V. Raghavachari,
learned Senior counsel for the respondent(s).
2. Though  the  order  dated  26.08.2025  is  not  on
record, however after perusing the materials on record
and hearing learned counsel for the parties, we are of
the view that despite notice being served, petitioners
1

--- Page 176 ---
refused to appear and contest the proceedings. However,
the Division Bench of the High Court, on principles of
equity,  has  set  aside  the  ex-parte  decree  dated
05.12.2023 and has restored suit, subject to deposit of
50%  of  the  decreetal  amount  while  condoning  the
inordinate delay of 457 days in filing the condonation
application for setting aside the ex-parte decree.
3. In such circumstances, we do not find any error or
infirmity with the view taken by the High Court.
However, by the impugned judgment and order dated
30.03.2026, the High Court had granted a period of 30
days for deposit of 50% of the decreetal amount,
failing which it was stated that the appeal pending
before  the  High  Court  would  stand  automatically
dismissed.
4. For ends of justice, we modify the quantum of
deposit from 50% to 40% of the decreetal amount and
extend the period of deposit of 40% of the decreetal
amount by a further period of six weeks from today.
5. Subject to the above, the Special Leave Petition
is disposed of.
6. Pending  application(s),  if  any,  shall  stand
disposed of.

          UPON hearing the counsel, the Court made the following
                             O R D E R
1. Heard learned counsel for the petitioner and perused
the material available on record.
2. The  petitioner  was  apprehended  while  being  in
possession of 5000 tablets of Tramadol Hydrochloride,
which is a narcotic drug as provided under the Schedule
1

--- Page 222 ---
SLP (CRL.)  NO.  11516/2026
to the Narcotic Drugs and Psychotropic Substances Act
(NDPS Act). The quantity of the contraband recovered is
much more than the commercial quantity prescribed under
the  Schedule.  The  petitioner  has  three  criminal
antecedents, of which, two are under the NDPS Act. In
this background, we are not inclined to enlarge the
petitioner on bail.
3. The Special Leave Petition is dismissed being devoid
of merits.
4. The Trial Court is directed to expedite the trial and
shall try to conclude the same within a period of 18
months from the date of receipt of copy of this order.
5. Copy of this order shall be transmitted to the Trial
Court forthwith.
6. Pending application(s), if any, shall stand disposed
of.

For Petitioner(s): Mr. Arjun S, Adv.

For Respondent(s): Mr. V. Philip Mathew, Adv.
          UPON hearing the counsel the Court made the following
                             O R D E R
1. We have heard learned counsel for the petitioner-
husband and learned counsel for the respondent-wife.
2. We find that the challenge before the High Court
was to the interim order dated 29.04.2026 passed by the
Family  Court,  Pathanamthitta,  whereby  the  interim
custody  of  the  minor  child  was  granted  to  the
petitioner-husband from 18.05.2026 to 22.05.2026.
3. This was challenged by the respondent-wife before
1

--- Page 306 ---
the High Court and the High Court vide order dated
19.05.2026, stayed the aforesaid order while fixing
22.06.2026 as the next date for filing counter by the
respondent-wife.
4. We find from the materials on record that the
custody petition filed by the respondent-wife is still
pending before the Family Court and the aforesaid
petition is also pending before the High Court.
5. In such circumstances, we are not inclined to
interfere in the matter.
6. However, we make it clear that the observations
made by the High Court in the order 19.05.2026 is only
for the purpose of passing the aforesaid order and
would have no bearing on the outcome of the proceedings
either before the Family Court or before the High
Court. Any further application(s) filed by the parties
shall be decided on their own merits.
7. With this observation, the Special Leave Petition
is disposed of.
8. Pending application(s), if any, shall also stand
disposed of.
(ABHINAV KUMAR)                                 (SAPNA BANSAL)
COURT MASTER (SH)                             COURT MASTER (NSH)

[Arising out of impugned final judgment and order dated 28-01-

Judicature at Allahabad]
ANIL SINGH                                      PETITIONER(S)
                                VERSUS
STATE OF U.P & ANR.                             RESPONDENT(S)
FOR ADMISSION 
IA No. 177343/2026 - CONDONATION OF DELAY IN REFILING /  
CURING THE DEFECTS
IA No. 177345/2026 - EXEMPTION FROM FILING O.T.
 
Date : 24-06-2026 This matter was called on for hearing today.
CORAM : 
         HON'BLE MR. JUSTICE UJJAL BHUYAN
         HON'BLE MR. JUSTICE ARUN PALLI
[PARTIAL COURT WORKING DAYS BENCH]
For Petitioner(s) :Mr. Rajeev Singh, AOR
                   Mr. Ashutosh Srivastava, Adv.
                   Mrs. Abhipsa Mohanty, Adv.                 
                   
For Respondent(s) : 
        UPON hearing the counsel the Court made the following
                             O R D E R
1. We have heard learned counsel for the petitioner and have
also perused the impugned judgment and order dated 28.01.2026.
2. Delay condoned.
3. Learned counsel for the petitioner while assailing the
impugned judgment and order of the High Court, which has
quashed the complaint, following submission of closure report
by the police, has placed reliance on a three-Judge Bench
1

--- Page 318 ---
decision of this Court in “Kishore Kumar Gyanchandani Vs. G.D.
Mehrotra and Another”,  reported in (2011) 15 Supreme Court
Cases 513, paragraph No.6 of which reads as under:
“6. It is too well settled that when police
after investigation files a final form under
Section 173 of the Code, the Magistrate may
disagree with the conclusion arrived at by the
police and take cognizance in exercise of power
under Section 190 of the Code. The Magistrate
may not take cognizance and direct further
investigation in the matter under Section 156
of the Code. Where the Magistrate accepts the
final form submitted by the police, the right
of the complainant to file a regular complaint
is  not  taken  away  and  in  fact  on  such  a
complaint being filed the Magistrate follows
the procedure under Section 201 of the Code and
takes cognizance if the materials produced by
the  complainant  make  out  an  offence.  This
question has been raised and answered by this
Court in the case of Gopal Vijay Verma v.
Bhuneshwar Prasad Sinha¹ whereunder the view of
the Patna High Court to the contrary has been
reversed. The Court in no uncertain terms in
the  aforesaid  case  has  indicated  that  the
acceptance of final form does not debar the
Magistrate from taking cognizance on the basis
of  the  materials  produced  in  a  complaint
proceeding.”
4. Issue notice, returnable on 17.08.2026.
5. In addition to the normal mode of service, permission is
granted  to  serve  the  standing  counsel  for  respondent
No.1/State of U.P.
     (SOURAV PAL)                             (SAPNA BANSAL)
SENIOR PERSONAL ASSISTANT                  COURT MASTER (NSH)
2
